# Changelog

All notable changes to Kronn will be documented in this file.

Format: [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/).
Versioning: [Semantic Versioning](https://semver.org/spec/v2.0.0.html).

---

## [Unreleased]

### Fixed

- **`AiDocViewer` no longer shows "no project documentation" on a failed fetch.** A failed `list_ai_files` request was caught silently and rendered the *same* empty-state message as a genuinely-undocumented project ŌĆö so a transient 500/network error looked like "this project has no docs". A failed load now shows a distinct error + **Retry** button (i18n FR/EN/ES), separate from the empty state (+2 tests). Detection itself was verified correct (the `ai/` ŌåÆ `docs/` pivot works end-to-end). Follow-up architecture captured in `TD-20260627-configurable-docs-dir` (make the docs root configurable: global default + per-project override).

## [0.8.9] - 2026-06-27

### Fixed ŌĆö Document generation works out of the box in Docker ("Document sidecar unavailable")

The PDF/DOCX/XLSX/PPTX feature spawns a Python sidecar (FastAPI + WeasyPrint/python-docx/XlsxWriter/python-pptx) from `~/.kronn/venv/docs`. The skill advertised "no external install needed", but the backend Docker image never created that venv ŌĆö so clicking a generated document returned `503 Document sidecar unavailable. Run \`make docs-setup\`ŌĆ”`, a manual step that makes no sense in the containerized stack. The image now **bakes the venv** (`backend/Dockerfile`): WeasyPrint's runtime libs (Pango/HarfBuzz + fonts) via apt, then `pip install` of the sidecar into `/home/kronn/.kronn/venv/docs`. That path isn't a mounted volume (compose only mounts the `~/.kronn/user-context` subdir), so it survives at runtime where `$HOME=/home/kronn`. Apply with a backend image rebuild (`docker compose build backend && docker compose up -d`). Non-Docker installs (desktop / bare `make start`) still use `make docs-setup`.

### Fixed ŌĆö Toggling a boolean setting OFF no longer fails ("├ēchec de la mise ├Ā jourŌĆ”")

The shared `api()` client built its request body with `if (body)` / `body ? ŌĆ” : undefined`, which treats `false`, `0` and `""` as "no body". So a `POST` carrying a falsy primitive sent an **empty body with no JSON content-type** ŌĆö and the backend's `Json<bool>` extractor 422'd it. Visible symptom: **disabling the continual-learning toggle** (`POST false`) failed while enabling (`POST true`) worked. Fixed by gating on `body !== undefined` instead, so only a genuinely-absent body is omitted. This silently affected every `Json<bool>`/falsy-primitive endpoint, not just continual learning. Regression tests pin `false`/`true`/no-body request shapes.

### Fixed ŌĆö Uploads over 1 MB no longer 413 at the gateway ("fichier trop volumineux")

`files-by-message-on-disc` (0.8.8) raised the backend's axum `DefaultBodyLimit` to 64 MiB, but the nginx **gateway** had no `client_max_body_size` directive ŌĆö so it applied nginx's **1 MiB default** and rejected any context-file upload over ~1 MB with a 413 *before the request ever reached the backend*. Added `client_max_body_size 64m` at the gateway `server` level (`.docker/nginx.conf`) to match the axum limit. The config is volume-mounted (not baked), so applying it is just `docker compose restart gateway` ŌĆö no rebuild.

### Fixed ŌĆö Whole-DB export now carries Quick APIs, learnings & global context

Migrating a Kronn install to another box (e.g. WSL ŌåÆ macOS) via Settings ŌåÆ *export ZIP* silently dropped data added since the 0.3.2 export was written. Closed the gaps that hurt a real migration:

- **Quick APIs** (`quick_apis`, migration 045) and **continual-learning rows** (`learnings`, migration 063) are now collected by `build_export` and re-inserted by `do_import_db`. Before, they were never in the payload.
- **`global_context`** (the cross-project instruction block injected into every agent prompt) travelled in the exported `config.toml` but `merge_import_config` never re-applied it ŌĆö now merged (with its mode) when the import carries one.
- `DbExport` payload bumped `version: 3 ŌåÆ 4`. All new fields are `#[serde(default)]`, so **v3 exports still import** (empty vecs). New tests: exportŌåÆimport round-trip for Quick APIs + learnings, global-context re-apply, and v3 back-compat deserialization.
- **Known residuals** (tracked in tech-debt): QP version *snapshots* (per-version metrics auto-recompute from discussions), uploaded `context_files` blobs (on disk, not in the ZIP), and secrets (API keys + MCP env) which stay stripped by design and must be re-entered.

### Added ŌĆö Remap a project whose folder is missing (the import's missing half)

After a cross-OS import, every project path is invalid (`/home/...` Ōćä `/Users/...`). The import toast said "remap them in the Projects page" ŌĆö but that page had no remap affordance, and the toast was ephemeral. Wired it end-to-end:

- **`Project.path_exists`** ŌĆö computed by `enrich_audit_status` (list/get API layer, not persisted). A missing directory also short-circuits the filesystem scans + self-heal writes that were pointless (and unsafe) on a gone path. The DB row mapper defaults it `true` so non-enriched reads (e.g. the export payload) never false-flag.
- **Per-card remap banner** (`ProjectCard`) ŌĆö always visible (even collapsed) when `path_exists === false`: an inline path input + "Remap" button calling the existing `POST /projects/:id/remap-path` (which validates the new path exists and rejects `..`). The previously-orphaned `projectsApi.remapPath` client now has a caller.
- **Page-level banner + filter** (`ProjectList`) ŌĆö persistent "N projects have missing folders" summary with a one-click "show only these" toggle to triage a large import.
- i18n FR/EN/ES. Tests: backend `enrich_audit_status` (missing ŌåÆ flagged + scans skipped, existing ŌåÆ present); frontend remap banner (render gating, call shape, trim, inline error, no-refetch-on-error) + list banner (singular/plural/filter).

### Added ŌĆö Continual Learning (0.9.0, behind a default-OFF beta toggle)

Agents can propose **durable learnings** (conventions, preferences, facts, pitfalls) that a human validates before they're persisted into injected truth files ŌĆö closing the "every discussion re-explains the same context" gap. Full design + the multi-agent review that hardened it: `docs/research/continual-learning-0.9.0-spec.md`.

- **Master toggle `continual_learning_enabled` ŌĆö default OFF (beta).** The feature writes agent-proposed content into injected docs, so it ships opt-in: a bug can't pollute a user's docs. Settings ŌåÆ *Apprentissage continu* (`ContinualLearningSection`) + endpoints `GET/POST /api/config/continual-learning-enabled`. Gates capture only ŌĆö validating/rejecting existing pending candidates stays allowed when off.
- **Typed MCP tool `learning_propose(claim, evidence[], kind)`** (no free-form fence) ŌĆö evidence is mandatory; disc/project/agent auto-inherited from the current discussion.
- **Two-gate verification.** Gate-1 (existence, reuses `core::anti_halluc::verify_source_marker`) runs at propose AND re-runs at validate against the current code. Gate-2 (faithfulness `claim ŌŖ© evidence`, `FaithfulnessChecker` trait) is **informative, never auto-blocking (posture B)** and **default OFF** ŌĆö a throwaway NLI proto on 255 real pairs (`docs/research/nli-proto-findings.md`) showed local NLI isn't reliable enough untuned; LLM-judge is the quality backend when enabled.
- **Write-path safeguards (all enforced backend, hardened across a 5-round adversarial review by a second agent):** non-empty evidence ┬Ę secret-guard (`core::redact`) ┬Ę `fact` ŌćÆ Ōēź1 `Verified` file/code evidence ┬Ę `preference` ŌćÆ Ōēź1 dated `user` evidence ┬Ę post-render re-lint refuses any fabricated `[src:]` BEFORE writing ┬Ę `validate` only promotes `pending` rows ┬Ę promoted entries carry re-lint-safe `[src:]` provenance ┬Ę negative-learning (3-strike, partial unique index so rejected claims can re-accumulate) ┬Ę confidence haircut ┬Ę anti-generalization warning.
- **Doc-wiring** (`core::learning_doc`, mirrors the anti-hallu STEP machinery): when ON, a `<!-- kronn:section name="learnings" -->` pointer to `docs/learnings.md` is injected into `docs/AGENTS.md` (so agents discover project-scope learnings ŌĆö verified that `docs/` isn't auto-injected, only `~/.kronn/user-context/*.md` is) + the file is seeded; when OFF, the section is removed (the file is kept). Endpoint `POST /api/projects/{id}/learnings/sync`.
- **Staleness cron** (`core::learning_sweep`, hourly, `COALESCE(last_validated_at, created_at)` ŌłÆ 7d) spawned in BOTH `backend/src/main.rs` and `desktop/src-tauri/src/main.rs`.
- **UI**: pending-count badge in `ChatHeader` (polls; opens a validation modal) + `LearningsModal` (type chip, confidence, evidence list, Gate-2 chip when present, Validate/Reject). i18n FR/EN/ES.
- Migration `063_continual_learning` (`learnings` + `learning_rejections`). ~65 backend + frontend tests; reviewed clean over 5 rounds (Ōēł18 findings, all addressed). *Remaining (optional, not blocking): manual-archiveŌåÆmodal intercept; wiring the LLM-judge backend; SSE-driven badge.*

### Added ŌĆö `kronn start-dev`: one-command native launch (no Docker)

- **New CLI command `./kronn start-dev`.** Runs Kronn **natively** ŌĆö backend + Vite with hot-reload ŌĆö in a single command, driving the **host** CLIs with their real logins. This is the macOS path (Docker can't execute Darwin binaries nor read the Keychain) and a fast dev loop on every platform. Previously this meant two manual terminals (`make dev-backend` + `make dev-frontend`); those still work and `start-dev` simply orchestrates them.
- **Preflight** checks the toolchain (`cargo` / `node` / `pnpm`, plus `cargo-watch`) and prints targeted install hints for whatever is missing instead of failing cryptically. The "what's missing" logic is a pure, unit-tested helper (`dev_missing_tools` in `lib/ui.sh`). It also **prepends the standard toolchain dirs** (`~/.cargo/bin`, `/opt/homebrew/bin`) to `PATH` for the checks and the spawned `make` children ŌĆö so it finds rustup's `cargo` even when the user never sourced `~/.cargo/env` in their shell rc (the common "works in one shell, not another" trap), and the backend it launches inherits the right `PATH`.
- **Prints the correct URL.** The backend serves **API-only on :3140** in native mode ŌĆö the UI is Vite on **:5173**. `start-dev` shows `UI ŌåÆ http://localhost:5173` explicitly so you don't open :3140 and get a blank page (a common Docker-habit trap; in Docker the gateway serves the UI on :3140). It also detects a Docker Kronn already bound to :3140 and warns before the port clash.
- **Backend startup banner is now native-dev aware.** `start-dev` exports `KRONN_DEV_UI_URL`, and the backend's `ŌåÆ` banner line points there (the Vite UI) instead of its own API port, with a "this port is the API only" note ŌĆö previously the banner always advertised `ŌåÆ http://ŌĆ”:3140`, contradicting the `:5173` the launcher prints. Logic extracted to `main.rs::banner_entry_url` (3 unit tests); unchanged in Docker (the gateway serves the UI on that port) and for a bare `make dev-backend`.
- **Clickable UI link (OSC 8 hyperlinks).** The UI URL is emitted as an OSC 8 terminal hyperlink ŌĆö clickable in Terminal.app, iTerm2, **Windows Terminal / WSL**, WezTerm, kitty, VS Code, etc. ŌĆö in both the `start-dev` launcher line (`lib/ui.sh::hyperlink`) and the backend's post-banner line (`main.rs::osc8_link`/`osc8`). **Not macOS-specific**: gated only on stdout being a TTY, so piped/redirected output (CI, logs) keeps the plain URL with no escape bytes. +5 tests (2 Rust `osc8`, 3 bats `hyperlink`).
- **Auto-opens the browser** to the UI once Vite is actually serving (polls `:5173`, then opens via `lib/ui.sh::open_url` ŌåÆ `open`/`wslview`/`xdg-open`, cross-platform). This is the reliable path because **macOS Terminal.app has no OSC 8 support**, so the clickable link never works there ŌĆö the browser open does. Opener selection is the pure, tested `pick_opener` (+4 bats tests). Opt out with `KRONN_NO_OPEN=1`.
- **Fix: `kronn start-dev` crashed on exit with `backend_pid: unbound variable`.** The cleanup trap referenced a `local` that was already out of scope when the `EXIT` trap fired (after the function returned) under `set -u`. Now a script-global PID + `${:-}` guard ŌĆö teardown is robust whether the trap fires on Ctrl+C or at exit.
- **Fix: the "Create a symlink in ~/.local/bin?" prompt reappeared on every launch** even once created, when `~/.local/bin` isn't on the user's PATH (`ensure_in_path` only checked PATH resolution). It now detects an existing symlink that points at this checkout and silently adds the dir to PATH for the session instead of re-prompting. Decision extracted to the pure `lib/ui.sh::path_link_action` (+4 bats tests).
- Backend runs in the background, frontend in the foreground; `Ctrl+C` stops the frontend and a trap tears down the backend so no detached `cargo-watch` is leaked.
- Cross-platform (Linux/WSL/macOS) ŌĆö no OS gating. Listed in `kronn help`, `docs/install.md` (macOS native section), and `docs/AGENTS.md`. +7 bats tests (`tests/bats/ui.bats`, suite 205 ŌåÆ 212).

### Changed ŌĆö Ollama first-pull suggestions refreshed + hardware-aware

- **Fixed a bogus suggestion (`gemma4:26b` ŌĆö never existed in the registry)** and refreshed the hardcoded first-pull list (`OllamaCard.tsx`) against `ollama.com/library`. The new list spans the **hardware range** ŌĆö Kronn also runs on no-GPU Windows/WSL boxes, not just powerful Macs: `llama3.2:1b` (~1.3 GB, CPU) ŌåÆ `llama3.2` ŌåÆ `qwen3:4b` ŌåÆ `qwen2.5-coder:14b` ŌåÆ `gemma3:27b` ŌåÆ `qwen3:30b` (MoE, ~19 GB).
- **Each suggestion now carries a hardware-tier badge** (`CPU Ō£ō (no GPU)` / `Ōēź 16 GB RAM` / `GPU or Ōēź 32 GB`) so users don't pull a 19 GB model onto an 8 GB laptop. Model descriptions moved from a hardcoded French string to i18n (FR/EN/ES).
- **The canirun.ai "can my hardware run this?" link is now a prominent clickable callout** (was a faint footnote-style link) with stronger copy, surfaced right where models are picked.
- Suggestions list exported + covered by tests (`OllamaCard.models.test.ts`: no `gemma4`, real tags, a CPU-tier option, every descKey/tier label resolves in all three locales).

---

## [0.8.8] - 2026-06-21

### Added ŌĆö `kronn start` warns on macOS that Docker can't run host CLIs (points to native)

A Docker container on macOS runs in a Linux VM and **cannot execute the user's host CLIs** (Darwin binaries can't run in the Linux container; agent OAuth creds live in the macOS Keychain, unreachable from the container). So `kronn start` on a Mac would spin up a stack that can't actually run agents ŌĆö confusing. `cmd_web` now detects macOS (pure `is_macos_host` in `lib/ui.sh`) and, before launching Docker, explains the limitation and points to the native paths (**desktop app** for solo use, or **`make dev-backend` + `make dev-frontend`** for hot-reload dev), then asks whether to continue in Docker anyway (web UI + API still work). Skippable with `KRONN_SKIP_MACOS_WARN=1`. **Linux/WSL are untouched** ŌĆö Docker is the right path there (host binaries are Linux and run directly in the container via the mount / `via_wsl`); a bats test pins that WSL/Linux are never flagged. 4 new `ui.bats` tests.

### Fixed ŌĆö RTK detection reported the container's binary, hiding the "install on host" flow (macOS)

`rtk_binary_available()` did a plain `which rtk`, which under Docker finds the container's **baked** `/usr/local/bin/rtk` and always returns `true`. So the RTK card showed "Activate" (never "Install"), the "Activate on all" wired hooks against the container's rtk ŌĆö useless for the host CLIs where the user actually runs agents ŌĆö and `rtk` stayed `command not found` in their terminal. Same container-vs-host mismatch as the agent-install fix: Kronn is the bridge; RTK belongs on the **host**.

- `rtk_binary_available()` is now **host-aware**: under Docker it checks the host bins (`KRONN_HOST_BIN`, already mounted) for `rtk`; native (Tauri/CLI) keeps `which`. So on a Mac without host-side RTK it correctly returns `false` ŌåÆ the existing CompressionSection **Install** button + curl modal appear, guiding the user to install RTK on their machine (where the hooks, written to the bind-mounted `~/.claude`/`~/.codex`/`~/.gemini`, then actually resolve `rtk` and `rtk gain` works).
- **Symlink-aware** (the Mach-O-launcher trap again): a Homebrew-installed `rtk` is a symlink into `../Cellar/rtk/<v>/bin/rtk`, and the host Cellar isn't mounted ŌĆö so the link dangles in the container and `exists()` (which follows symlinks) returned false even though RTK was installed. The check now accepts a symlink entry via `symlink_metadata()` too. Verified live: after `brew`-installing RTK on the host, detection flips to `rtk_available=true` and the agents show `RTK actif`.
- Regression test `rtk_binary_available_in_docker_checks_host_bins` (hermetic via `KRONN_DATA_DIR` + `KRONN_HOST_BIN`; covers empty / real-file / dangling-symlink). clippy `-D warnings` clean, rtk_detect suite green (13).

### Added ŌĆö New-discussion form warns (red) when launching an agent without active RTK

When you launch an RTK-capable agent (Claude Code / Codex / Gemini CLI) from the new-discussion form and RTK isn't active for it, shell output isn't compressed ŌåÆ noticeably more tokens consumed. The form now shows a **red alert at the top**: *"RTK n'est pas actif ŌĆö vous risquez de consommer plus de tokens que n├®cessaire"* + a link to enable it (Config > Agents). Skipped for non-RTK agents (Kiro/Copilot/Vibe/Ollama) and when RTK is active (`rtk_available && rtk_hook_configured`).

- `RTK_APPLICABLE` + `isRtkActive()` extracted to `lib/constants.ts` as the single source of truth (CompressionSection now imports them instead of its own copy).
- `NewDiscussionForm.tsx` gates the alert on `launchAgentNow && RTK_APPLICABLE.has(agent) && !isRtkActive(agent)`; red `.disc-rtk-warn` mirrors the amber `.disc-restricted-warn`. i18n FR/EN/ES (`disc.rtkWarn` / `disc.rtkWarnLink`).
- 3 new `NewDiscussionForm` unit tests (shows when no RTK / hides when active / hides for non-applicable agents); `tsc` clean, 147 frontend tests green. Verified live via Playwright (open new-discussion ŌåÆ red alert visible).

### Fixed ŌĆö `kronn-internal` MCP was dropped from projects that had no other MCPs

`sync_project_mcps_to_disk` (`core::mcp_scanner`) **deleted** a project's `.mcp.json` (+ `.kiro/`, `.gemini/`, `.ai/mcp/`) whenever the project had no user-linked MCPs ŌĆö so the auto-injected `kronn-internal` introspection bridge (57 tools: `disc_get_message`, `disc_summarize`, ŌĆ”) only ever reached projects that *also* had at least one other MCP. A project with only Kronn's own bridge (the common case) lost it entirely: agents in its discussions had no introspection. The MCP server itself was fine (verified via an `initialize` + `tools/list` handshake) ŌĆö it just wasn't being written to disk.

- The empty-MCP branch now **writes a `kronn-internal`-only** `.mcp.json` (+ Kiro/Gemini/.ai variants) instead of deleting them, via a new `write_kronn_internal_only()` (mirrors `write_general_mcp_json`). Only `.vibe/config.toml` is still removed (Vibe has no bridge ŌĆö it's prompt-injection fallback). When the bridge path can't be resolved (host-CLI safety), stale files are still cleaned up.
- Regression test `empty_project_still_writes_kronn_internal_only` (drives the bridge path via env so it's hermetic in any build env). Verified live: `POST /api/mcps/refresh` on an MCP-less project now produces a `.mcp.json` carrying `kronn-internal` (gitignored).

### Added ŌĆö The built-in `kronn-internal` MCP is now visible (read-only) on the Plugins page

`kronn-internal` (the discussion-introspection MCP, `python3 disc-introspection-mcp.py`) is auto-injected into every project's agent configs at sync time (`core::mcp_scanner::inject_kronn_internal`) ŌĆö but it was never surfaced in the UI (it's in neither `builtin_registry()` nor the DB), so users couldn't tell it existed. It now shows as a **read-only "system" card on the main Plugins view** (`data-testid="mcp-kronn-internal-card"`), visible directly ŌĆö not behind the "Ajouter" catalog ŌĆö and even with zero configured plugins: `Plug` icon, name "Kronn Internal", *Int├®gr├®* badge, description "auto-injected into every project ŌĆö nothing to install or configure", tooltip, **no add/config/link flow**. Pure frontend (no backend/registry change), so it can never be instantiated/linked or collide with the auto-injection. i18n FR/EN/ES (`mcp.builtin.*`). Validated by a `McpPage` unit test (card present on the default view, no interaction) **and** a real Playwright E2E against the running app (navigate to Plugins ŌåÆ card visible without clicking Add).

### Fixed ŌĆö A quota/plan-limit error shows a clean message, not a 32 KB stderr dump

When an agent exits on a recognised error (Codex "You've hit your usage limitŌĆ”", quota, auth, rate limit, MCP), the discussion now **leads with the clean, actionable hint** and folds the raw agent output into a collapsible "d├®tails techniques" card (reuses the `kronn:context` marker) ŌĆö instead of burying the real signal under a wall of echoed prompt + stderr. The quota detector was widened to catch Codex's exact wording ("usage limit", "purchase more credits", "upgrade to pro") and now surfaces the provider's "try again at <time>" in the message. +2 backend tests (Codex usage-limit wording + retry-time extraction).

### Changed ŌĆö Non-streaming agents free their concurrency slot faster when hung (clog fix)

The 2026-06-23 fix let non-streaming agents (Codex `exec` etc.) bypass the short stall and rely on the 30-min global timeout ŌĆö but a genuinely-hung run then squatted one of the 5 `agent_semaphore` slots for the full 30 min. After a day of large batch fan-outs, the slots clogged and everything queued ("planted"). Non-streaming agents now use a **bounded 15-min stall** (`NON_STREAMING_STALL_TIMEOUT`) ŌĆö comfortably above a real run (1-3 min) but half the global window, so a hung run releases its slot in reasonable time. Test pins it's between the streaming stall and the global. *(Restarting the backend clears an existing clog instantly.)*

### Added ŌĆö Persistent "N agents running" badge ŌĆö in-flight runs stay visible after you navigate away

Agent runs are server-side; the live view is an SSE bound to the discussion you're looking at. Leaving the page (or just switching tabs) closed that SSE, so the UI stopped *showing* progress ŌĆö making it look like nothing was running, which tempted re-launching a workflow that was in fact still going (especially batch fan-outs, whose background children you never opened). New `GET /api/discussions/running` returns the disc ids with an in-flight run RIGHT NOW, sourced from the existing cancel registry (every run registers a `CancelGuard` there for its whole lifetime ŌĆö removed on ANY exit, so no ghost state). The Dashboard polls it every 5 s from its persistent shell and shows a **"ŌÅ│ N en cours" badge in the nav** (click ŌåÆ discussions), independent of any SSE ŌĆö so a still-working run keeps showing regardless of where you navigate. Kept as a separate state from the live `sendingMap` on purpose (feeding the poll into it would trip the stale-stream watchdog, since background children produce no local chunks). +1 backend integration test (route precedence + registry reflection + `CancelGuard` Drop clears it) + 1 frontend api test. FR/EN/ES.

### Added ŌĆö Injected context (a ticket, a fileŌĆ”) renders as a collapsible card, distinct from the agent's instructions

When a Quick Prompt / batch step injects a large value into the agent message (e.g. a whole Jira ticket ŌĆö description + comments + linked issues ŌĆö substituted into a `{{var}}`), the result was one undifferentiated markdown blob: the static instructions and the injected payload looked identical, so you couldn't tell "what Kronn told the agent to do" from "the ticket it pasted in". Now the substitution wraps any large injected value (Ōēź 400 chars) in a `kronn:context` marker (an inert HTML comment ŌĆö invisible to the agent), and `MessageBubble` renders each marked block as a **collapsible "­¤ōŗ Injected context ┬Ę <var>" card** (collapsed by default, accent-bordered, expands to the markdown-rendered payload) while the instructions stay normal markdown. Small values (a date, an id) stay inline. Backend `wrap_injected_context` (in the QP/batch renderer) + frontend `splitInjectedContext` / `MessageBody` / card. Backward-compatible (old messages have no marker ŌåÆ render unchanged). +6 backend unit + 6 frontend unit tests. FR/EN/ES.

### Changed ŌĆö Agent prompt no longer dumps every API's full endpoint catalogue (big context-bloat cut)

Every agent run injected, for **every** configured REST API plugin (Chartbeat, Adobe, JIRA, customsŌĆ”), the API's **entire endpoint list** + a curl example + inlined credentials ŌĆö into the system context, **even when the agent never touched an API**. On a multi-plugin project that's tens of KB of dead weight on every single run (and it's what made some discussions balloon). It's also fully redundant with the `api_call` MCP broker (which already knows the endpoints and injects auth server-side) and `mcp_list` (on-demand discovery). `build_api_context_block` now emits a **lean** per-API summary ŌĆö name, base URL, auth, an endpoint **count** + the first endpoint as a shape example, and a pointer to `api_call` / `mcp_list` for the rest ŌĆö instead of the whole catalogue. Direct curl stays possible (auth/config still inlined, docs linked); the agent just isn't force-fed every path it'll never call. Test rewritten to pin the lean shape (count + one example + tool pointers, second endpoint NOT dumped).

### Fixed ŌĆö A huge message no longer crashes the browser tab (two layers + a real-browser regression test)

Opening a discussion whose reply was multi-megabyte (a killed agent that left a 2.4 MB stderr/reasoning dump as its message) froze then **crashed the tab**: the content went through ReactMarkdown + remark-gfm + syntax highlight, which are super-linear and blew up the heap. Fixed at both ends so it can't recur:

- **Source (backend):** the streaming loop already capped stdout at `MAX_AGENT_RESPONSE_BYTES` (2 MB), but the error/kill path **replaced** the response with the full captured stderr ŌĆö uncapped. A single char-boundary-safe cap (`cap_agent_response`) now runs at the persistence boundary, so EVERY path is bounded and no multi-MB message reaches the DB.
- **Render (frontend):** `MarkdownContent` guards on size ŌĆö past ~200 KB (far above any normal reply) it renders the message as **plain text** (markdown disabled), truncated inline with a notice showing the real size, so even a legacy/oversized row already in the DB opens instantly instead of crashing.

Tests: +3 backend unit (`cap_agent_response`: untouched under limit, capped + marker over, UTF-8 boundary-safe) ┬Ę +3 frontend unit (normal markdown unchanged; oversized ŌåÆ plain text + notice + truncation) ┬Ę +1 **real-Chromium perf spec** (`large-message-render.perf.spec.ts` + `seed_large_message.py`) that opens a seeded 3 MB-message discussion and asserts the guard banner appears within budget ŌĆö jsdom can't catch a real OOM, so this closes the gap that let the bug ship. FR/EN/ES.

### Fixed ŌĆö Workflows now work with every agent, not just Claude (non-streaming agents were silently killed)

A workflow whose Agent steps ran on **Codex / Vibe / Gemini / Kiro / Copilot / Ollama** could finish with empty discussions while the *same* workflow worked perfectly on Claude. Two root causes, both in the agent lifecycle:

- **The stall watchdog assumed streaming.** Only Claude runs with `--output-format stream-json` (`OutputMode::StreamJson`) and emits a chunk every few hundred ms; **every other agent is `OutputMode::Text`** and writes its answer *only at the very end* ŌĆö legitimately silent on stdout for the whole run. The watchdog that kills an agent after N minutes of "no output" was meant for a hung stream, but it killed slow-but-healthy non-streaming runs before they could produce their single end-of-run reply. Non-streaming agents now bypass the stall and rely on the absolute global deadline (`effective_stall_timeout`). Claude's short stall is unchanged.
- **Empty children counted as successes.** A batch (fan-out) child that exited cleanly but produced an *empty* reply was counted as `completed`, so a batch workflow reported a green **Success** over discussions that were all blank ŌĆö hiding the failure entirely. A child now counts as a success only with a clean exit **and** a non-blank response (`child_run_counts_as_success`), so `failed` reflects reality and an all-empty batch surfaces as Failed.

Verified live that Codex itself works in the container (slow, but a real reply on stdout); the failure was Kronn's pipeline assuming streaming. +5 unit tests (stall mapping per output-mode, empty/whitespace/failed-exit child accounting); Claude streaming path covered by a pin test so it can't regress.

### Added ŌĆö Exec steps accept stdin input (`exec_stdin`) ŌĆö large payloads no longer hit the argv limit

An `Exec` step received its input only through `exec_args`, and a single argv string is capped at ~128 KB by the OS (`ARG_MAX`). A reshaped payload (e.g. an enriched ticket backlog) blew past that around ~16 items and failed to spawn with *"Argument list too long"*. Exec steps now take an optional **`exec_stdin`** (templated like `exec_args`) piped to the main command's stdin ŌĆö no size ceiling. The payload is streamed on a detached task so stdout/stderr drain concurrently (no pipe deadlock on a large bidirectional command like `jq`/`cat`). `None` ŌåÆ stdin stays `/dev/null` (unchanged). +5 unit tests (delivery, full-payload-past-argv, large bidirectional no-deadlock, templating, null backward-compat); exposed in the MCP `workflow_create_draft` step example.

### Fixed ŌĆö Live-run step label no longer claims "the agent is starting" on a deterministic step

In a workflow's live run, an `ApiCall`/`Exec`/`Gate`/`Notify` step in progress showed *"L'agent d├®marreŌĆ” (aucun chunk re├¦u)"* ŌĆö wrong, those steps have no agent. The placeholder is now type-aware: only `Agent` steps show the streaming-wait copy; every other type shows a neutral "step runningŌĆ” (output appears when it finishes)" (`liveStepWaitingKey`). +10 frontend unit tests. FR/EN/ES.

### Changed ŌĆö The MCP server now ORIENTS the agent (what Kronn is + a tool map), so it stops reverse-engineering capabilities

The `kronn-internal` MCP returned `initialize` instructions, but they only covered the API-reuse order ŌĆö nothing said *what Kronn is* or gave a map of the 40+ tools. So an agent built its mental model by reading tool descriptions piecemeal, and **generalised the system's abilities from whatever sample it happened to open** (a real incident: it `workflow_get`-opened a workflow with only `Agent` steps and concluded SubWorkflow/Exec/TypedSchema didn't exist). The instructions now lead with a concise orientation ŌĆö what Kronn does + the tool surface by area (Discussions ┬Ę Workflows ┬Ę Quick Prompts ┬Ę Quick APIs/broker ┬Ę docs ┬Ę learning) + per-area pointers (`workflow_get` = full, `qp_get` = full incl body, `workflow_create_draft`'s description = the step schema) + a **navigation rule**: *to understand a capability, read the tool's description AND `*_get` a REAL rich example ŌĆö never infer the system's abilities from one sample.* Kept concise (a closed map + pointers, not a manual; open catalogues stay behind on-demand tools). `workflow_create_draft` now also enumerates the full closed `step_type` set (Agent ┬Ę ApiCall ┬Ę BatchApiCall ┬Ę BatchQuickPrompt ┬Ę Exec ┬Ę Gate ┬Ę Notify ┬Ę JsonData ┬Ę **SubWorkflow**) with a SubWorkflow example. +2 tests pin the orientation coverage + the step-type taxonomy (a new `StepType` shipping undocumented fails the test). Python-only ŌåÆ live without rebuild.

### Added ŌĆö Attach a file ON DISK (not inlined): big files (HAR, logs, datasets) the agent reads with its tools

Uploading a non-image file previously **extracted its text into the agent's context** (capped at 500KB, and rejected outright above it / above axum's ~2MB request-body limit). So a 5MB HAR couldn't be attached, and even smaller text files cost their full size in tokens every turn. Files now land **on disk** and only a short preview is inlined ŌĆö the agent reads/parses the full file (or loads it in a headless browser) by path, with zero whole-file token cost. Three parts: **(1)** the context-files upload route accepts up to **64MB** (was ~2MB); **(2)** any non-image, non-office file is saved raw to `.kronn/context-files/` in the discussion's worktree and surfaced as `--- name (file on disk) --- <path> + preview (first 8KB)` instead of full inline text (images still go to disk with vision instructions; office docs ŌĆö xlsx/docx/pptx/pdf ŌĆö still convert to inline text since their raw binary isn't readable); **(3)** the agent gets the path + an explicit "read the full file with your tools" instruction. Small files (Ōēż8KB) are still fully visible via the preview. Also hardened the frontend upload: a 413/non-JSON response now surfaces a clear "fichier trop volumineux" toast instead of a generic parse-error message. Backend + frontend; +9 tests.

### Added ŌĆö MCP: workflow run history, per-run detail, and cancel

The MCP could only see a workflow's *active* runs (`workflow_active_runs`) or latest run ŌĆö there was no way to list a workflow's **run history**, drill into a finished run's per-step results, or cancel a run (the UI's "Arr├¬ter" had no MCP equivalent). So an agent debriefing a scheduled workflow (how many runs, which failed, which step) was stuck, and couldn't stop a stuck/duplicate run. Three wrappers over existing REST routes (python-only, live without rebuild): **`workflow_runs(workflow_id, limit?)`** ŌĆö lean history, most-recent-first (status ┬Ę run_type ┬Ę timings ┬Ę tokens ┬Ę batch counts ┬Ę `parent_run_id`); **`workflow_run_get(workflow_id, run_id)`** ŌĆö full per-step detail (durations, status, kind, truncated output) for debriefing a failure; **`workflow_cancel_run(workflow_id, run_id)`** ŌĆö stop a running run. Foreach/batch children are enumerable by calling `workflow_runs` on the *child* workflow's id and filtering on `parent_run_id`. +7 tests.

### Changed ŌĆö MCP `workflow_create_draft` defaults a Cron/Tracker workflow to `concurrency_limit: 1` (no accidental self-overlap)

A Cron workflow drafted without `concurrency_limit` had no overlap guard: if a run outlasted the next scheduled tick, the scheduler started a *second* run on top of the first (the engine only skips a tick when `active_runs Ōēź concurrency_limit`, and `None` means no check). Real incident ŌĆö a ~2.5h PR-review cron fired its next-hour tick while still running, so two runs processed the same PRs in parallel (double work + risk of duplicate reviews). The MCP `workflow_create_draft` tool now defaults `concurrency_limit` to **1** for `Cron`/`Tracker` triggers when the agent doesn't set it (mirroring the existing `enabled: false` safety default; an explicit value still wins, so overlap is opt-in). The tool's field docs + the `workflow-architect` skill now explain the self-overlap footgun at the trigger-decision point, and clarify that a blocked tick is **skipped, not queued**. Python-only (live without rebuild); +3 tests.

### Added ŌĆö BatchApiCall accepts `{{item.<field>}}` as a per-item accessor alias

A `BatchApiCall` already exposed each item's fields as `{{batch.item.<field>}}` and bare `{{<field>}}` (templatable in `api_endpoint_path`, body, query, headers) ŌĆö but agents intuitively reach for `{{item.<field>}}`, which wasn't set, so a per-item path like `/comments/{{item.commentId}}/reactions` kept the placeholder literal and 404'd. `inject_item_vars` now also sets `item.<field>` (and `item` = the whole item) as a forgiving alias, so `{{batch.item.commentId}}`, `{{item.commentId}}`, and `{{commentId}}` all resolve. The MCP `workflow_step_schema` (BatchApiCall.PER_ITEM_VARS + template_vars) and the `workflow-architect` skill now document the accessor and flag that it differs from a SubWorkflow-foreach item (`{{current_task.*}}`).

### Added ŌĆö Workflow templating injects a nested array/object into an `api_body` (deterministic LLMŌåÆAPI piping)

An `Agent` step could emit a structured result (`output_format: TypedSchema`), but a downstream `ApiCall` couldn't put a nested array/object from it into its JSON body: `render_json_value` rendered every string leaf through the template engine, so `"comments": "{{steps.review.data.inlineComments}}"` became an escaped **string**, not a real array ŌĆö GitHub's review API (and any typed API) then 422'd. And `{{steps.X.data_json.<field>}}` didn't resolve at all (the nested resolver only anchored on the `data` alias, not `data_json`), leaving the placeholder literal. Both fixed: (1) the nested resolver now anchors on `data` OR `data_json` (aliases), and a new typed resolver returns the actual `serde_json::Value`; (2) in an `api_body`, a field whose value is **exactly one** `{{ŌĆ”}}` placeholder pointing at structured data is replaced by the **real typed JSON** (arrays/objects/numbers preserved). It stays injection-safe ŌĆö a parsed `Value` is re-serialized, never spliced as raw text, so a `"}` inside the data still can't break out of its field; a placeholder embedded in surrounding text (`"PR #{{n}}"`) still string-renders. So a reviewŌåÆpost pipeline now works in one call: `api_body: { "event": "{{steps.review.data.verdict}}", "body": "{{steps.review.data.generalComment}}", "comments": "{{steps.review.data.inlineComments}}" }`. +7 unit tests (`template`, `api_call_executor`). MCP `workflow_step_schema` (Agent.OUTPUT_PIPING + template_vars) and the `workflow-architect` skill document it.

### Added ŌĆö MCP: a foreach SubWorkflow exposes the current item as `{{current_task.<field>}}` template vars

A SubWorkflow `foreach` child could only reach the current item by **reading the file** `.kronn/current_task.json` ŌĆö the only templatable handle was `{{__subwf_item_id__}}` (the item's `id`). So an agent that wanted the PR number in an ApiCall path (`/pulls/.../reviews`) had no working accessor and kept guessing `{{current_task.number}}` / `{{item.*}}` / `{{foreach.*}}`. The engine now flattens each top-level field of the item into the child's `trigger_context` as `{{current_task.<field>}}` (scalars stringify, `null`ŌåÆempty, nested arrays/objects ŌåÆ compact JSON, whole item = `{{current_task}}`) ŌĆö so `/repos/o/r/pulls/{{current_task.number}}/reviews` and a worktree `.kronn/pr-{{current_task.number}}` just work. The accessor name is **fixed `current_task.*`** (it mirrors the file, *not* `{{item.*}}`, *not* the source-file name); the file remains the full-object fallback. Pure helper `current_task_template_vars` + 2 unit tests. The MCP `workflow_step_schema`, `workflow_create_draft` description, `steps` schema field, and the `workflow-architect` skill all document both paths.

### Fixed ŌĆö MCP `workflow_create_draft`/`workflow_update` now accept a bare-string `step_type` (was a 422 trap)

`WorkflowStep.step_type` is a serde internally-tagged enum (`#[serde(tag = "type")]`), so the wire form is a tagged object `{"type":"Agent"}`, not a bare string `"Agent"` ŌĆö but the MCP examples showed the bare string, so an agent copying them hit an opaque `422 invalid type: string, expected internally tagged enum` (the exact reverse-engineering-by-422 loop the MCP CRUD tools were meant to kill). The Python wrapper tests never caught it because they mock the HTTP layer (never hit serde). Fixed: `workflow_create_draft`/`workflow_update` now wrap a bare-string `step_type` (and `output_format`, `mode`) into the tagged `{"type": ŌĆ”}` form before POSTing ŌĆö both forms work, and the canonical tagged form (what `workflow_get` round-trips) is now used in every tool example + the `workflow_step_schema` `shape`/`steps` docs. Python-only (live without rebuild); +5 tests.

### Added ŌĆö MCP: full CRUD for the Agent-step bindings (skills ┬Ę profiles ┬Ę directives)

The `kronn-internal` MCP had no way to enumerate ŌĆö let alone author ŌĆö the skills/profiles/directives an Agent step binds via `skill_ids`/`profile_ids`/`directive_ids`; the `workflow_create_draft` description just pointed at "the workflow-architect skill for the canonical lists" with no tool to read them. Now there's a full CRUD surface, all thin wrappers over REST routes the UI already uses (python-only ŌåÆ live without a rebuild):

- **`skills_list` / `profiles_list` / `directives_list`** ŌĆö lean catalogs (id ┬Ę name ┬Ę description ┬Ę category; the markdown/persona body is dropped) so an agent can PICK valid binding ids instead of guessing or asking the user to paste them.
- **`skill_create` / `skill_update` / `skill_delete`** (+ `profile_*`, `directive_*`) ŌĆö author, edit (load-merge-write, category-validated), and delete **custom** entries (builtins are protected server-side). So an agent can now retain ┬Ę retrieve ┬Ę evaluate ┬Ę modify the skills it relies on. ŌÜĀ A skill update remints the id (the backend recreates it) ŌĆö the returned object carries the new id.
- **`workflow_step_schema`** ŌĆö the canonical WorkflowStep schema as a tool **result** (never truncated, unlike a long tool description): the closed 9 `step_type`s, per-type required/optional fields + examples, and the run-breaking runtime contracts (the SubWorkflow foreach contract in particular). Some MCP clients truncate long tool descriptions mid-text, which had been hiding the foreach contract ŌĆö this is the untruncatable source. The `workflow_create_draft` description was also trimmed (4.7 KB ŌåÆ ~3.9 KB), a 7-vs-9 `step_type` inconsistency in its "Discovery first" block was fixed, and the foreach contract duplicated into the `steps` schema field as a truncation backstop.

+19 Python tests (`StepSchemaAndBindingListTests`, `AgentLibraryCrudTests`); full MCP suite 197 green; 54 tools total.

### Added ŌĆö MCP can now read ┬Ę clone ┬Ę update ┬Ę enable workflows & Quick Prompts (not just create)

The `kronn-internal` MCP could only **create** workflow/QP drafts. An agent iterating an existing workflow had no way to read its steps (`workflow_list` is a compact summary), clone it, or patch it ŌĆö so it reverse-engineered the `WorkflowStep` schema from a chain of 422s and left an orphan QP behind every time it recreated a prompt instead of patching it. Six new tools close the loop, all thin wrappers over REST routes the UI already uses (so they ship as a python-only change, live without a backend rebuild):

- **`workflow_get(id)`** ŌĆö the FULL definition (every step + field), unlike the compact list.
- **`workflow_clone(id, new_name?)`** ŌĆö duplicate via exportŌåÆimport (mints fresh ids, re-bundles + rewrites referenced QP ids, strips per-user notify URLs). The clone lands **DISABLED** with a distinct `(copie)` name so it never auto-fires and you never get two identically-named workflows.
- **`workflow_update(id, patch)`** ŌĆö true patch (omitted fields preserved; `steps` replaced wholesale ŌĆö fetch via `workflow_get`, edit, send back).
- **`workflow_set_enabled(id, bool)`** ŌĆö disable is always allowed; enabling a **Cron/Tracker** workflow is refused unless `force=true` (it would schedule autonomous runs with no human in the loop), Manual enables freely.
- **`qp_get(id)`** ŌĆö the FULL Quick Prompt, including the `prompt_template` body that `qp_list` drops (and all bindings). So an agent can read what a QP *does* ŌĆö to run it itself, or to read it before a `qp_update` surgery. `qp_list` says a QP exists; `qp_get` says what it does. (Closed a real gap: `qp_list` dropped the body and there was no `qp_get`, so agents had to ask the user to paste the QP.)
- **`qp_update(id, patch)`** / **`qp_delete(id)`** ŌĆö load-merge-write patch over `qp_list` + delete, so a QP can be iterated in place instead of orphaning a copy.

Also: `_normalize_variables` fills `PromptVariable`'s required `label`/`placeholder` so agents can pass `{name}` alone instead of 422-ing (wired into both `*_create_draft` handlers too), and `workflow_create_draft`'s description now embeds a correct **flat WorkflowStep** example (Agent / ApiCall / Exec / Gate / Notify / BatchQuickPrompt) so the step schema is discoverable at call time. +21 Python tests (`WorkflowQpCrudToolTests`); full MCP suite 173 green. *(Deferred to 0.9.0: `workflow_validate` returning all errors at once ŌĆö the only piece needing a Rust change, since the create/update validator is fail-fast.)*

### Fixed ŌĆö `api_call` broker silently forwarded malformed JSON bodies (opaque target 400s)

When an agent's `api_call` `body` looked like JSON but didn't parse (an LLM brace/quote slip ŌĆö e.g. one extra trailing `}`), the broker's `json.loads` failed and it **silently forwarded the raw string**, so the target API got a JSON-quoted string and replied `400 Invalid request payload` ŌĆö reading like a body truncation when the body was in fact complete. The broker now **fails loud** on a JSON-looking-but-invalid body with an actionable error (char count, "NOT truncated", points at the JSON itself) instead of forwarding it. Python (live without rebuild) + a Rust defense-in-depth check (`json_body_error` in `agent_api.rs`, +4 unit tests) on the same path.

### Fixed ŌĆö Citation verifier false positives (46% ŌåÆ 12% non-verified)

The anti-hallucination linter flagged ~46% of agent citations as non-verified ŌĆö and a survey of real agent discussions found the flagged files **provably exist on disk**. Three root causes, all fixed in `core::anti_halluc`:

- **Backtick parser bug** ŌĆö agents write a markdown path with the line spec *outside* the backticks (`` `path`:line ``). `clean_reference` ran before `split_path_and_lines`, so the closing backtick was internal at clean-time, survived, and got appended to the path ŌåÆ `stat` failed. Now the post-split path is re-cleaned (trim-only, still SSRF-safe).
- **App-subdir paths** ŌĆö a project whose code lives under a subdir (front_euronews: `application/`) made every path the agent cites relative to the *app* root (`apps/x/Foo.php`) miss at the *project* root. New **segment-aligned, unique-only path-suffix walk** resolves `apps/x/Foo.php` ŌåÆ `application/apps/x/Foo.php`. Guards: heavy/`.kronn` dirs pruned, 60k-entry cap, and **only a unique match verifies** (2+ ŌåÆ ambiguous, never a false verify).
- **Cross-repo citations** ŌĆö `finalize_lint_report` now also resolves against the project's declared `linked_repos` (filesystem locations), so an agent citing a sibling repo (`front_apollo/ŌĆ”`) isn't flagged. No new mounts (repos under `$HOME` are already visible at `/host-home`); a linked repo that isn't present is skipped (stays soft-unverified, never errors).

Measured on the same workflow before/after: **verified 55% ŌåÆ 87%, false-positive "couldn't verify" warnings 44% ŌåÆ 12%**, with **fabricated count unchanged at 0** (no false verifies introduced). The 12% residual is legitimate ŌĆö repos not wired into Kronn, wildcard paths, API endpoints, ambiguous basenames, and a genuine out-of-bounds line. Principle: *couldn't-verify ŌēĀ fabricated*. Diagnosis hardened by a multi-agent expert panel + a code-grounded fact-checker. +10 unit tests.

The per-message lint pill also no longer **hides the good news**: when the headline is a warning (e.g. "1 affirmation sans source") but the reply also has verified citations, a second green "N v├®rifi├®e(s)" chip now shows alongside it (both open the same detail drawer) ŌĆö so the footer reflects the real ratio instead of only the worst signal. +4 frontend tests.

### Fixed ŌĆö Dashboard froze on "Almost readyŌĆ”" under agent load

`GET /api/setup/status` (which the dashboard boot blocks on) ran a full agent-detection sweep on **every** call ŌĆö spawning `<binary> --version` per installed agent. Under concurrent-agent load (a running batch/workflow) those spawns stalled, the endpoint hung, and the whole app sat on "Almost readyŌĆ”" forever ŌĆö the user's "nothing happens when I launch my workflow". Three layers of fix:

- **Cache** the detection sweep (60s TTL; invalidated on install/uninstall) so it isn't re-run on every boot.
- **4s hard budget** on the sweep (`detect_all_cached`) ŌĆö on overrun it serves the stale cache (or a fast degraded empty), so `setup/status` can never hang even on a cold cache under load.
- **Frontend timeout-and-proceed** (`App.tsx`): the boot request is now timed out (a hung promise fires neither `.then` nor `.catch`), and after retries the app proceeds optimistically when a fast endpoint confirms the backend is reachable ŌĆö only a genuinely unreachable backend shows the error screen.

+2 backend cache tests, +2 App boot tests (hangŌåÆproceed, hang+downŌåÆerror).

### Added ŌĆö Per-message attachments (images & files pinned to the message that carries them)

Until now an uploaded file was linked to the whole **discussion**: it stayed "sticky" in the composer, never appeared in the sent message bubble, and had to be deleted by hand. Files now attach to the **message** they were sent with, and images render as thumbnails in that message's bubble.

- **Schema** ŌĆö migration `066_context_files_message_id` adds a nullable `context_files.message_id` (+ index); `067_context_files_backfill_legacy` stamps pre-existing rows with an inert `__legacy_disc_wide__` sentinel so old disc-wide files aren't vacuumed into the next message sent. `NULL` = pending (still in the composer); non-NULL = pinned.
- **Link-on-send** ŌĆö `send_message` pins every pending file of the discussion to the new user message (`link_pending_context_files_to_message`, scoped + idempotent). The creation popup (`NewDiscussionForm`) uploads *after* the first message exists and runs via `run_agent` (which doesn't link), so a new `POST ŌĆ”/context-files/link-pending` endpoint + a frontend call pin popup uploads to the **first** message.
- **In-bubble rendering** ŌĆö new `MessageAttachments` component: image thumbnails fetched as **auth'd blobs** (an `<img src>` can't carry the auth header) ŌåÆ object URL, filename chips for non-images. `DiscussionsPage` splits pending (composer) vs attached-by-message; the attachment binds the instant you send (an `onStart` disc reload swaps the optimistic id for the real one) instead of only after the agent finishes.
- **Image byte route** ŌĆö `GET ŌĆ”/context-files/{file_id}/content` streams the bytes for the thumbnail. Path is resolved from the DB row keyed by **both** discussion_id and file_id (no client-supplied path ŌåÆ no traversal); the `Content-Disposition` filename is stripped of quotes + control chars.
- **MCP exposure (end-to-end)** ŌĆö `disc_get_message` (current disc) **and** `disc_load_other` (cross-disc) now return `attachments[] {id, filename, mime_type, disk_path}`, so an agent browsing any thread can discover an image's on-disk path and open it with its file tools. `disc_search` is unchanged (disc-level; you `disc_load_other` into the hit). Proven live: a cross-disc read returned all images of a thread, each openable via the returned `disk_path`.
- i18n FR/EN/ES (`disc.attachmentImage`). Tests: 6 DB-layer unit (link scoping/idempotence, per-message list, message_id round-trip, 067 backfill) + 1 MIME-map unit, 11 integration (content route bytes + 404 matrix incl. cross-disc, filename header-injection sanitize, MCP `disc_get_message`/`disc_load_other` attachments, link-pending endpoint, persistent-dir), 5 frontend unit (`MessageAttachments`) + 3 api-method (`linkPendingContextFiles`, `contextFileBlob` ok/throw), 3 browser E2E (hermetic render + real popup-first-message + real DOCROMS_WEB agent upload). clippy `-D warnings` clean.

### Fixed ŌĆö Context-file images were served with the wrong MIME (rendered as text on click)

`mime_from_extension` had no image cases, so every `.png/.jpg/ŌĆ”` was stored as `text/plain`. Harmless while the MIME only fed a display label, but once the byte route served images for thumbnails, the browser (with `X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff`) rendered them as text when opened full-size. Added the image MIME map **and** made the content route derive the type from the filename ŌĆö so legacy rows already stored as `text/plain` serve correctly without a DB backfill. +1 unit, +1 integration regression test.

### Fixed ŌĆö Images on project-less discussions were lost on every restart

Uploads on a discussion with no project fell back to `std::env::temp_dir()` ŌĆö the container's `/tmp`, wiped on every restart/rebuild, so the bytes vanished and bubble thumbnails 404'd. They now persist under the data dir (`config_dir()` / `KRONN_DATA_DIR` volume), dropping to temp only if that can't be resolved. +1 integration test asserting the saved path lives under the data dir, not temp. *(Pre-existing project-less images whose bytes were already in the old `/tmp` are unrecoverable ŌĆö their rows 404.)*

### Changed ŌĆö Backend coverage floors raised + first tests on the real orchestrator/TOCTOU/chat loop

A test-coverage pass (pure additions, no production code touched) closed structural holes: the **first** tests driving the real workflow runner end-to-end (`execute_run` via deterministic `JsonData` steps ŌåÆ persisted PendingŌåÆRunningŌåÆSuccess + failure path), a multi-attempt sequence harness over the real anti-hallu citation gate, the TOCTOU `claim_waiting_run` (was zero-test), and the **first** browser `{page}` E2E on the discussion chat loop (type ŌåÆ send ŌåÆ SSE chunks ŌåÆ bubble; prior disc specs were all `{request}` API-only). Measured coverage then locked in: backend CI floors raised to **lines 78 / functions 82 / regions 80** (from 77/81/78); a stale `DiscussionSidebar.grouping` fixture was corrected to the `non_system_message_count` contract.

### Added ŌĆö Anti-hallucination `enforce` mode (PR-A audit gate ┬Ę PR-B disc refusal ┬Ę PR-C beta)

`AntiHallucMode::Enforce` previously behaved exactly like `warn`. PR-A gives it teeth on the **audit pipeline** ŌĆö the surface that writes the most durable docs.

- **Per-step citation gate** (`api/audit/anti_hallu_enforce.rs`, pure + unit-tested): in `enforce`, after an audit step's agent writes its `docs/` file, the file's formal `[src: ŌĆ”]` markers are mechanically re-linted against the real tree (`core::anti_halluc::analyze_roots`). A fabricated citation (path missing / line out of bounds / outside project / training-data) **re-runs the step** with a corrective addendum naming the broken citations (bounded by `MAX_ATTEMPTS = 3`, new `step_retry` SSE event). If they still don't resolve after the cap, the step fails ŌåÆ the run ends *Interrupted* (no validation discussion) instead of committing a doc with invented citations.
- **Auto-stamp `audit="<today>"`** on every `curated="ai"` section of a clean step file (idempotent, deterministic, 0 tokens) ŌĆö the date honestly reflects "verified conformant today".
- `off`/`warn` are unchanged: one attempt per step, gate inert. The gate's branching is a pure `decide(verdict, attempt, max) -> Pass|Retry|Fail` so it's unit-tested without a live agent. 12 new unit tests; clippy `-D warnings` clean.

PR-B extends `enforce` to **discussions** (chat / batch / WF agent steps), at the runner chokepoint + the streaming finalize:

- **Auto-attached `kronn-doc-author` skill.** When `enforce` and the agent's project carries a `docs/AGENTS.md`, the doc-authoring cheat-sheet (`kronn:section` markers + `[src:]` grammar) is injected inline so any agent that edits docs writes in the convention the lint accepts ŌĆö even if the user never attached the skill. Idempotent (skipped when already in `skill_ids`), inert outside enforce.
- **Non-destructive P3 fail-fast.** When a finalized agent reply carries a fabricated `[src:]` citation, the message is **kept** (with its red pill) and a System note is appended (`Ōøö R├®ponse refus├®e (enforce) : N citation(s) fabriqu├®e(s) ŌĆ”`) so the human arbitrates a correction. No auto-retry ŌĆö on a user disc the user decides.
- Both branches are pure, unit-tested policies in `core::anti_halluc` (`should_auto_attach_doc_author`, `enforce_refusal_needed`, `enforce_refusal_message`); 3 new tests. clippy `-D warnings` clean.
PR-C lifts the `enforce` mode out of preview: the Settings label is now **Strict (beta ┬Ę 0.8.8)** (FR/EN/ES) and the help text + selection toast ŌĆö which still claimed *"behaves like Warn until 0.8.8, write-refusal ships then"* ŌĆö now describe what `enforce` actually does (audit step-retry ŌåÆ clean fail; disc reply kept but flagged). The enforce feedback is already visible through existing surfaces (the disc refusal renders as a System message; an exhausted audit gate surfaces as a `step_warning` in the audit recap). *Optional remaining polish: a live `step_retry` chip during an audit, and extending the existing checksum drift banner with the anti-hallu signals (audit date > 6 mo, unresolved `[src:]`).*

### Fixed ŌĆö Feasibility AutoPilot `run_tests` PHP verdict reported ERROR(harness) on a healthy suite

The parent `run_tests` step mounted the project's `vendor/` conditionally, gated by a fragile hostŌåÆcontainer path back-substitution (`${vend/#ŌĆ”}`); when it mis-evaluated, `vendor/` was left unmounted ŌåÆ phpunit couldn't autoload ŌåÆ boot failure mis-classified as `ERROR(php harness)`. Now vendor is resolved by checking the **container** paths directly (worktree's own `vendor/` first, else borrow main's), and a genuinely absent `vendor/` is an honest **SKIP (run composer install)** instead of a scary ERROR. Also added `--colors=never` so the `Tests: N` / `Failures:` summary parse is ANSI-free. Verified live on front_euronews (3602 tests ŌåÆ PASS; filtered class ŌåÆ clean OK). +4 assertions on the existing `run_tests` template test.

### Fixed ŌĆö Sidebar message count inflated by System rows

The "N msg" label in the discussion sidebar (`SwipeableDiscItem`) and on the dashboard `ProjectCard` showed the raw `message_count`, which counts tool-call breadcrumbs, cached-summary lines and the new enforce-refusal note (all `MessageRole::System`) ŌĆö wildly higher than the real conversation length. The 0.8.7 fix had switched the unread *badge* to `non_system_message_count` (via `unseenBasis`) but the visible total label was missed. Both now use `unseenBasis(disc)` (the backend already exposes the System-excluding count via a subquery). Render-level regression test added.

### Fixed ŌĆö Auto-summary kept firing after being disabled in Settings

`maybe_generate_summary` only checked the **per-disc** `summary_strategy`, which is frozen at creation from the global default. Turning auto-summary off in Settings only affected NEW discs, so older long threads (created when the default was `Auto`) kept summarising. The global `default_summary_strategy` is now a **master kill-switch**: `SummaryStrategy::auto_fires(global, disc)` returns false whenever the global is `Off`, regardless of the disc's frozen value; otherwise the per-disc strategy decides as before. Pure + unit-tested.

### Fixed ŌĆö Anti-hallucination: bare-filename citations no longer false-flagged

A dominant source of false "unverified" amber pills: an agent that cited a file by **bare name + line** (`` `NewslettersManager.ts:107` ``) without its full path was flagged unverified even though the file exists ŌĆö `verify_file_ref` only probed the path at each root's top level, so a nested file never resolved.

- `verify_file_ref` now falls back to a **unique-basename walk** when a separator-less name doesn't resolve at root level: exactly one matching file in the tree ŌåÆ `Verified` (with line-bounds check + the resolved relative path shown in the pill detail); 2+ matches ŌåÆ stays unresolved but with an actionable *"ambiguous, cite the full path"* reason; 0 ŌåÆ `NotFound` as before. Full paths are unchanged.
- The walk reuses the `scanner` skip-list (`node_modules`, `vendor`, `target`, **`.kronn`** ŌĆ”) ŌĆö skipping `.kronn` is load-bearing: its `worktrees/` hold full project copies that otherwise make every basename look ambiguous (real case: front_euronews had 11 copies of one file, 1 real). Multi-root (Isolated worktree + main) is first-root-wins, so a file present in both isn't double-counted as ambiguous. Bounded walk (caps at 60k entries ŌåÆ never a false unique on a partial scan).
- Verified live on the exact false positive (disc `d344b52b`): `NewslettersManager.ts:107` and `SocialLoginManager.ts:199` now resolve `Verified` against the real checkout. 8 new unit tests (incl. the `.kronn/worktrees` skip, ambiguity, multi-root, out-of-bounds, and the end-to-end inline-anchor case); clippy `-D warnings` clean.

### Fixed ŌĆö Kiro device-flow login no longer blocks every `kronn start`/`restart` on macOS

On macOS, `maybe_login_kiro` (`kronn`) launched an **interactive, blocking** Kiro device-flow login on every startup whenever `kiro-cli` was present-but-unauthenticated in the backend container. But `entrypoint.sh` installs a Linux `kiro-cli` **into the container** on macOS regardless of the user's host setup ŌĆö so its presence says nothing about whether the user uses Kiro, and a Claude-Code-only user was nagged at every launch for an agent they never installed.

- Kronn is now **completely silent about Kiro by default** ŌĆö no prompt, no hint. The device-flow login (and any Kiro message at all) is **opt-in only** via `KRONN_KIRO_LOGIN=1`, which makes Kronn probe the container and run `make kiro-login` when unauthenticated.
- Decision logic extracted to a **pure, testable** helper `kiro_startup_action(os, authenticated, available, opt_in)` in `lib/agents.sh`; `maybe_login_kiro` only probes (and only when opted in) and runs the docker-exec side effects.
- **Cross-platform unchanged**: the flow was already macOS-only (`return 0` elsewhere) ŌĆö non-Darwin and the default (no opt-in) both return `skip`, so Windows / WSL / Linux behaviour is byte-for-byte identical, and the Tauri desktop launcher is unaffected.
- 6 new bats tests in `tests/bats/agents.bats` cover the matrix (incl. the regression: macOS + available + no opt-in ŌåÆ `skip`, never any output). Full shell suite green (201/201).

### Fixed ŌĆö Claude Code detected as "Exec format error" on macOS (Darwin binary picked over the Linux copy)

On macOS, the Settings ŌåÆ Agents panel showed Claude Code with the version `Cannot run macOS (Mach-O) executable in Docker: Exec format error` instead of a real version. Two compounding causes, both now fixed:

- **`find_binary` ignored the macOS skip list on its primary lookup** (`backend/src/agents/mod.rs`). The container `PATH` mounts the host's `~/.local/bin` (`/host-bin/local`), so `which::which("claude")` resolved the **Darwin** launcher; the `MACOS_HOST_BIN_SKIP` guard was only consulted in the fallback dir-scan, never on the `which` path. Version detection then exec'd the Darwin binary ŌåÆ "Exec format error". The skip decision is now a pure `should_skip_darwin_host_binary(name, host_managed, host_is_macos)` consulted on **both** resolution paths; a skipped Darwin binary falls through to the Linux copy / the `npx` runtime fallback (Claude Code is npx-probeable, same as Codex/Gemini). 4 new unit tests.
- **`entrypoint.sh` never installed the Linux Claude** because its `command -v claude` guard matched that same Darwin shadow on `PATH` and concluded Claude was already present. Replaced the boolean `command -v` guard with an **exec-free** `host_darwin_needs_linux_copy()` helper that returns true **only** when the binary resolves exclusively under the host mount (`/host-bin/*`) ŌĆö i.e. the user has it on their Mac and we mirror a runnable Linux copy (strongly preferred over the npx wrapper, which has crashed on long Claude sessions). Deliberately does **nothing** when the agent is absent everywhere, so Kronn stops silently installing agents the user never had (see the *Changed* entry below). Applied uniformly to `claude` / `codex` / `gemini` / `copilot` / `kiro-cli`.

clippy `--all-targets -- -D warnings` clean; the agents-module unit suite passes (30/30 in the relevant filter).

### Changed ŌĆö Agents the user never installed are no longer shown as "Activ├®" (Setup Wizard + Settings)

The Setup Wizard (`SetupWizard.tsx`, the pre-config screen on first launch) and Settings ŌåÆ Agents (`AgentsSection.tsx`) both treated `runtime_available` (npx-reachable) as "installed": any npx-runnable agent got the enable/disable toggle and read **Activ├®/D├®sactiv├®**, even though the user never installed it. Combined with `entrypoint.sh` auto-installing `kiro-cli` into the container, a Mac user who had installed **only Claude Code** saw Codex/Gemini "Activ├®", Copilot "D├®sactiv├®", and Kiro as installed ŌĆö none of which they'd installed.

- **npx ŌēĀ installed.** Only an agent actually installed in the container now gets the enable/disable toggle. An npx-only agent shows the **Install** button instead, keeping its `runtime OK ŌĆö via npx` hint so the "still usable without installing" info isn't lost. The status dot is green only for `installed && enabled`.
- **Kiro is no longer auto-installed** in the container (the `entrypoint.sh` change above): with nothing on the host, Kiro shows the **Install** button like any other not-installed agent. This also removes the root cause of the macOS Kiro-login nag (no `kiro-cli` present ŌåÆ nothing to log into).
- Net effect on a Claude-only Mac: Claude ŌåÆ installed (native Linux copy mirrored from the host install), everything else ŌåÆ **Install** offered. Exactly "only what I installed is installed".
- 2 frontend tests updated/added (`SetupWizard.test.tsx`, `AgentsSection.actions.test.tsx`); `tsc --noEmit` clean, both suites green (43 tests in the two files).

### Fixed ŌĆö npm-based agent install (Install button + boot mirror) failed with EACCES in the container

Installing an npm agent (Codex/Gemini/Copilot/Claude) ŌĆö via the **Install** button (`POST /api/agents/install` ŌåÆ `install_agent` ŌåÆ `npm install -g <pkg>`) or the macOS boot mirror in `entrypoint.sh` ŌĆö failed with `EACCES: permission denied, mkdir '/usr/local/lib/node_modules/...'`. The container runs as the non-root `kronn` user, but npm's default global prefix (`/usr/local`) is root-owned.

- **`backend/Dockerfile`** now sets `ENV NPM_CONFIG_PREFIX=/home/kronn/.local` (the user-writable dir already first on `PATH` and `chown`ed to `kronn`). Every `npm install -g` ŌĆö the Install button, the boot mirror, anything else ŌĆö now lands in `/home/kronn/.local/bin`. Declared *after* the build-time `npm install -g ccusage` so that root install is unaffected. Container-scoped: the Tauri/host build never uses this Dockerfile, so host npm installs keep their own prefix.
- The redundant per-call `--prefix` added to `entrypoint.sh` was dropped in favour of this single image-level source of truth.
- Verified end-to-end live: `POST /api/agents/install "CopilotCli"` ŌåÆ `{"success":true,"data":"added 4 packages"}`, and Claude/Gemini/Copilot resolve to `/home/kronn/.local/bin/<agent>` with real versions. (Image-level env + boot script ŌĆö no bats/Rust harness covers the Dockerfile; verified against the running container.)
- **Known follow-up (not fixed here):** button-installed agents live under `~/.local` which is **not** volume-backed, so they don't survive a container rebuild/`kronn restart` (Claude is re-mirrored at boot because it's on the host; the others would need a re-install or a persistent volume). Tracked separately.

### Fixed ŌĆö "Cannot connect to backend" (401) on Docker Desktop macOS once an auth token exists

`config.rs` generates an auth token on first launch (`auth_enabled = true`), relying on the `auth_middleware` localhost bypass to keep things transparent for self-hosted users. That bypass keys off the client IP (`is_local_ip`), but **Docker Desktop on macOS NATs every published-port request to the Docker network gateway** (e.g. `192.168.97.1`), which `is_local_ip` correctly refuses to treat as local (the `tailscale_lan_and_public_are_not_local` test pins that ŌĆö broadening it would let LAN peers skip auth). Result: once a token was generated, every API call from the browser got `401` ŌåÆ the UI showed "Cannot connect to backend".

- **`auth_middleware` now honours the `auth_enabled` master switch** (`backend/src/lib.rs`): when `auth_enabled = false`, auth is skipped entirely even if a token is still present in the config. This matches what `setup_status` already reported (`auth_enabled && token.is_some()`) ŌĆö the middleware was the only place ignoring the flag. Leaving the token in place keeps the switch sticky: `config.rs` only re-generates a token when none exists, so it never re-flips `auth_enabled` back to `true`.
- This is the supported escape hatch for the Docker Desktop macOS case (and any setup where the localhost bypass can't see the real client IP): set `auth_enabled = false`. `is_local_ip` is intentionally left untouched ŌĆö no security regression, no LAN bypass.
- Existing auth users are unaffected: token generation still sets `auth_enabled = true`, so the master switch is on for them by default.
- New integration test `auth_disabled_master_switch_bypasses_even_with_token` (`api_tests.rs`); the existing `auth_*` suite stays green (51 tests in the filter); clippy `--all-targets -- -D warnings` clean.
- **Durable default (fixes first-launch for *every* Docker user, not just an existing instance):** `core::config::load` now seeds `auth_enabled = core::env::auth_on_by_default()` (= `!is_docker()`) when it first generates the token, instead of unconditionally `true`. So a fresh config under Docker starts with auth **off** (token still generated, ready for opt-in multi-user) and never 401s on first launch; native (Tauri/CLI) keeps auth **on** (the localhost bypass works there). This survives `/data` resets ŌĆö without it, every regenerated config flipped auth back on and re-locked Docker-macOS users. **Security note:** an exposed multi-user Docker server now starts without auth and must enable it explicitly (`auth_enabled = true`). 2 new serial env tests (`auth_off_by_default_under_docker`, `auth_on_by_default_when_native`).

### Changed ŌĆö Agent "Install" is disabled under Docker (installs land in the container, not the host)

Under the Docker deployment, the backend runs in a Linux container that mounts the host bin **read-only** and cannot execute anything on the host ŌĆö so the "Install" button could only ever install *into the container*, never onto the user's machine. That surprised macOS users who installed an agent expecting `codex` to be runnable in their own terminal. The UI is now transparent about it.

- **`/api/health` exposes `in_docker`** (`backend/src/lib.rs`, raw JSON ŌĆö no ts-rs/typegen) from `core::env::is_docker()` (keyed on `KRONN_DATA_DIR`, set only by docker-compose/Dockerfile). Cross-platform verified: **Tauri/native ŌåÆ `false`** (`KRONN_DATA_DIR` unset), Docker (macOS/Linux/WSL) ŌåÆ `true`.
- **Setup Wizard + Settings ŌåÆ Agents**: when `in_docker`, the **Install button is disabled** (tooltip shows the host install command) and a **warning note** points users to install on the host via the `kronn` CLI. Native/Tauri keeps Install fully functional (installs on the host). Threaded as an `inDocker` prop (default `false` ŌåÆ no behaviour change off-Docker, all existing tests green).
- **Platform intent**: Docker on Linux/WSL ŌåÆ host install yields a Linux binary that Kronn runs via the read-only mount; Docker on macOS ŌåÆ host (Darwin) binaries can't run in the Linux container anyway, so the native macOS path remains the **Tauri desktop app**. Documented in `docs/AGENTS.md`.
- Tests: backend `health_exposes_in_docker_bool` (`api_tests.rs`); frontend `AgentsSection.actions.test.tsx` + `SetupWizard.test.tsx` (disabled + note when `inDocker`, unchanged otherwise); `App`/`SettingsPage` test mocks extended with `health`. clippy `-D warnings` clean, `tsc --noEmit` clean, 4 frontend suites green (68 tests).

---

## [0.8.7] - 2026-05-28

### Added ŌĆö Big-ticket AutoPilot: multi-agent debate + per-task testŌåÆfix loop (2026-06-13)

A major evolution of the `feasibility-autopilot`, validated live across 13 runs on a real Epic (AfricanewsŌåÆEuronews multi-brand migration). The plan is now **debated** by two agents and each fan-out task **fixes its own tests** before committing.

- **`multi_agent_review` ŌĆö debate the output of ANY Agent step with a second agent (new `WorkflowStep` field + `run_multi_agent_debate` engine).** After the step's own agent produces its output, Kronn opens a shared transcript and invites a reviewer agent (ideally a different model family); they alternate authorŌåöreviewer until `[CONSENSUS: APPROVED]` or `max_rounds`. The converged output replaces the step's result (envelope-safe: on a TypedSchema step the author re-emits the full envelope, a guard reverts to the pre-debate output if it can't). Exposed as an advanced option in the WorkflowWizard (reviewer agent + tier + debate prompt). The feasibility-autopilot wires it **onto its `triage` step** (reviewer = Codex), **replacing the old `plan_review ŌåÆ Goto(triage)` file-relay loop** ŌĆö the reviewer reads the artifact once then only the conversation delta, not the whole codebase each round: **ŌłÆ44 to ŌłÆ52 % on the plan phase** (197ŌĆō229k vs ~408k), and a real back-and-forth.
- **Per-task testŌåÆfix loop in the child (`item_tests`).** Each fan-out task runs the tests SCOPED to what it changed (`php -l` + `jest --findRelatedTests` + `phpunit --filter` in the project's dockerized php service) and, on a real failure, loops back to `implement` until green (bounded). **Baseline-aware** (`test_baseline` parent step records the tests already red on the approved base into `.kronn/known-failing.txt`): `item_tests` only loops on **NET-NEW** failures, never on the repo's pre-existing debt ŌĆö eliminating ~104k wasted tokens/run (agents stopped chasing a pre-existing timezone-test failure). The parent `run_tests` becomes a read-only full-suite integration verdict (JS in-container with coverageŌēĀtest-failure semantics; PHP via the project's docker stack, worktree-mounted).
- **Reliability hardening (all from live runs):** `[agents.model_tiers]` overrides now reach workflow agent spawns (were silently dropped) ┬Ę Codex always `--sandbox=danger-full-access` in Docker (bwrap can't init a namespace in the container ŌåÆ reviewer was blind) ┬Ę `request_changes_cut` resumes from the FIRST occurrence so a gate "request changes" after a Goto debate actually returns to triage ┬Ę `agent_retry` (2├Ś rate-limit-aware backoff) on the Agent steps ┬Ę workflow guard timeout 2 h ŌåÆ 8 h (a 26-item fan-out was killed before `pr_draft`) ┬Ę implement `stall_timeout` 20 ŌåÆ 10 min.
- **UI:** live fan-out progress on a Running SubWorkflow step (`N sub-tasks ┬Ę M Ō£ō` instead of "no chunk received") ┬Ę the resolved model/tier on every Agent step card (`StepResult.step_model`, e.g. `opus`, `sonnet ┬Ę reasoning`, `haiku ┬Ę economy` ŌĆö incl. per-item routing) ┬Ę fixed the per-task fan-out TABLE vanishing when a child output embedded a nested `---END_STEP_OUTPUT---` marker ┬Ę clickable sub-run link.
- Skill `workflow-architect` documents `multi_agent_review`. Design notes: `docs/design/collaborative-plan-review.md`, `docs/design/ew7247-autopilot-live-audit.md`. ~70 new/updated backend + frontend tests.

### Fixed ŌĆö Playwright MCP unusable for agents (wrong browser channel) (2026-06-11)

Agents (and anyone) couldn't drive a browser through Kronn's Playwright MCP: `mcp-playwright` launched `@playwright/mcp` with no `--browser`, so it defaulted to the **`chrome` channel** (real Google Chrome at `/opt/google/chrome/chrome`) ŌĆö almost never installed, even though `npx playwright install chromium` had downloaded the bundled browser. Every launch failed with "chrome not found" (disc f30e340d). The registry now pins `--browser chromium`; the boot registry sync + host_sync propagate the corrected args to existing configs' `.mcp.json`. Test pins it. **Anyone with the bundled Chromium can now run PW/browser steps.**

### Added ŌĆö `feasibility-autopilot` decomposed (PR-C) + in-flight board MCP tool (2026-06-11)

- **`feasibility-autopilot` decomposed** (frontend preset + backend `build_feasibility_workflow` + `templates/feasibility-autopilot` endpoint, kept in sync). Parent `fetch_issue ŌåÆ triage ŌåÆ review_triage(Gate) ŌåÆ [feasibility_impl sub-workflow] ŌåÆ pr_draft`; child `implement ŌåÆ run_tests ŌåÆ drift_check`. The human-gated triage stays in the parent; triage writes its manifest to `.kronn/triage-manifest.md` and the child reads it from the shared worktree (Phase 2). `pr_draft` reads `{{steps.triage.data}}` (parent) + the child's drift output via the SubWorkflow envelope (`{{steps.feasibility_impl.data.last_output}}`) + `.kronn/decisions.md`. The endpoint creates the child first, then the parent referencing its id. **Behaviour change**: the old `implement BLOCKED ŌåÆ Goto(triage)` (a cross-parent/child jump, now illegal) is reconstructed at the parent as `SUBWF_FAILED ŌåÆ Goto(triage)`; a mid-implement hard-block is otherwise traced (KRONN-TODO + decisions.md) and surfaced in the PR. Backend + frontend tests updated.
- **In-flight board MCP tool** `workflow_active_runs` (kronn-internal): lists every run that's NOT finished right now (Running / WaitingApproval / Pending) across all workflows, so an agent can see what else is happening before acting. Pure read over `GET /api/workflows` (no new endpoint); drill into a run's live step via `workflow_run_status`. Skill + 3 Python tests.

### Added ŌĆö Decomposed presets: SubWorkflow infra + worktree handoff + `ticket-to-pr` (2026-06-11)

Made `SubWorkflow` usable end-to-end by the AI path AND the templates.

- **Workflow Architect skill** now teaches **nine** step types (was eight): a full `SubWorkflow` section (role, schema, `OK`/`SUBWF_FAILED` signals, the 5 hard constraints, the create-child-first composition protocol). Guard test pins the count + `SubWorkflow` by name.
- **Bundle infra**: `POST /api/workflows/bundle` gains a `child_workflows[]` category; the `@bundle:<id>` sentinel now resolves on `sub_workflow_id` too. Children are created first (inheriting the parent's `project_id`) and the SubWorkflow-graph validator (cycle/depth/no-gate/dangling) ŌĆö previously skipped on the bundle path ŌĆö now runs over the in-memory bundle graph.
- **Phase 2 ŌĆö worktree handoff**: a sub-workflow child can now **share the parent's git worktree** (`execute_run` gained `inherited_workspace`): it attaches instead of creating, skips `before_run`, and never cleans up / preserves the branch (the parent owns it). The child commits to the parent's branch so a later parent step (`create_pr`) sees the implementation. Test pins the invariant (attach ŌåÆ drop without cleanup ŌåÆ worktree + commit survive ŌåÆ parent preserves the branch).
- The SubWorkflow step envelope now carries the child's last-step output (`data.last_output` / `last_step`) so a parent step can read the child's verdict.
- **`ticket-to-pr` preset decomposed**: parent `fetch ŌåÆ analyze ŌåÆ plan_gate ŌåÆ [implement-verify sub-workflow] ŌåÆ ready_gate ŌåÆ create_pr ŌåÆ notify`; child `implement Ōåö run_tests Ōåö review` (internal loop, no Gate). Both human gates kept. ParentŌåöchild data flows through `.kronn/plan.md` (intent) + `.kronn/decisions.md` (deviations) in the shared worktree ŌĆö no new step field.
